## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is the acceleration of an oscillator given position x, velocity v, and time t, which is characteristic of second-order ODE models for forced/damped nonlinear harmonic oscillators. Typical structures combine a restoring term in x (often nonlinear), a damping term in v (often nonlinear), and optional explicit time-dependent forcing or parametric modulation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (small-amplitude spring-mass with viscous damping)
- Driven linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Parametrically excited oscillator (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness / parametric resonance)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance and jumps)
- Pendulum (nonlinear restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (bounded restoring force for angular displacement)
- Driven pendulum: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator / phase locking)
- Van der Pol oscillator (state-dependent damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (self-excited oscillations / limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-nonlinear damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (negative damping at small |v|, positive at large |v|)
- Nonlinear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (amplitude-dependent dissipation)
- Amplitude-dependent frequency (soft/hard spring in rational form): dv_dt = -(c0 * x) / (1 + c1 * x**2) - c2 * v (restoring force that weakens with |x| or saturates)
- Smoothed dry friction + spring: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * tanh(c2 * v) (Coulomb-like friction opposing motion, regularized)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: conservative single-well oscillators typically have dv_dt as an odd function of x (e.g., -x, -x - x^3), indicating symmetric potential U(x).
- Conservative vs dissipative split: terms depending only on x often represent -dU/dx (energy storage), while terms depending on v represent dissipation or pumping (energy change).
- Damping sign structure: physical damping usually satisfies v * dv_dt_damp <= 0, suggesting damping terms like -c*v, -c*v*|v|, -c*v^3, or -tanh(c*v).
- Limit-cycle indicator: state-dependent damping such as (c0 - c1*x^2)*v or (c0 - c1*v^2)*v implies negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, yielding self-sustained oscillations.
- Nonlinear stiffness fingerprints: presence of x^3 (or higher odd powers) implies hardening/softening behavior and amplitude-dependent resonance frequency.
- Bounded restoring force: sin(c*x) suggests angular dynamics (pendulum-like) where restoring force saturates for large |x|, unlike polynomial springs that grow unbounded.
- External periodic forcing: additive cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) terms indicate driven oscillations, frequency locking, and resonance peaks in response.
- Parametric modulation: multiplicative time dependence in stiffness, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, suggests Mathieu-type instability tongues and parametric resonance.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (PO18)
============================================================
GT: -beta*sin(x)*v - omega0**c0*x
Candidate formulas: 67

GT is the fixed function
\[
f(x,t,v)= -0.583656039990477\, v\sin(x)\;-\;1.81264753578235\,x.
\]
So any matching candidate must be exactly “linear in \(x\)” plus “\(v\sin(x)\)” with the same coefficients, and **no** extra dependence on \(t\), no constants, no other nonlinear \(x\) terms, no extra \(v\) terms, etc. Phase shifts are allowed inside the sine: we need \(\sin(c\_a x + \phi)\) to equal \(\sin(x)\) for all \(x\), which forces \(c\_a=1\) and \(\phi=2\pi k\) (or \(c\_a=-1,\phi=\pi+2\pi k\) giving the same \(\sin(x)\)).

---

### 1. `c0*x + c1*v*sin(c2*x + c3) + c4*log(c5*x + 1) + x`
Set log term off: \(c4=0\). Then expression is \((c0+1)x + c1 v\sin(c2 x+c3)\). Choose \(c2=1, c3=2\pi k\) and \(c1=-0.583656...\). Choose \(c0+1=-1.812647...\Rightarrow c0=-2.812647...\). **Matches.**

### 2. `c0*x + c1*x + c2*v*sin(c3*x + c4) + c5*log(c6*x + 1)`
Set \(c5=0\). Then \((c0+c1)x + c2 v\sin(c3 x+c4)\). Choose \(c3=1, c4=2\pi k\), \(c2=-0.583656...\), and \(c0+c1=-1.812647...\). **Matches.**

### 3. `... + c5*t + c6`
To match GT (no \(t\), no constant), must set \(c5=0, c6=0\). Then reduces to candidate 2 form. Choose parameters as in (2). **Matches.**

### 4. `... + c4*t + c5 + x`
Need \(c4=0, c5=0\). Then \((c0+1)x + c1 v\sin(c2 x+c3)\). Choose as in (1). **Matches.**

### 5. `... + c5*v*(c6 + t)**c7`
GT has no such \(t\)-dependent factor. Only way is to kill it: \(c5=0\). Then reduces to candidate 2 form. **Matches.**

### 6. `... + c4*v*(c5 + t)**c6 + x`
Kill extra term with \(c4=0\). Then same as (1) without log. Choose \(c2=1,c3=2\pi k,c1=-0.583656...\) and \(c0=-2.812647...\). **Matches.**

### 7. `... + c4*x*(c5 + v)**c6 + x`
GT has no \(x\cdot g(v)\) term. Must set \(c4=0\). Then same as (1) core. **Matches.**

### 8. `... + c5*x*(c6 + v)**c7`
